asphalt mixture / modifiers) if necessary. One asphalt layer (the surface asphalt layer 
only) or more than one (Multiple Pass Operations) is laid to pave more than one layer. 
This method includes many advantages, including reducing transportation costs of 
materials and reducing traffic control work, due to the short treatment period and 
correcting surface distresses not caused by structural inadequacy such as rutting, 
raveling, cracks, and holes, but there are many challenges to this method, including: 
 Contractors need to purchase new, high-cost equipment that are capable of 
heating, scarifying asphalt surface layers, adding additives and raw materials 
if needed, mixing materials and paving. 
 This method is not suitable if rutting and cracks in the aged pavement layers 
are of high intensity. 
 Not suitable for existing pavement that includes rubber, geotextile and large 
size aggregates. 
 Low degree of compaction because temperatures drop rapidly from the 
minimum allowed. 
 Ride quality issues in the recycled layer and bleeding due to the irregular 
addition of materials. 
 The occurrence of many problems during the operation of the equipment at the 
site, such as irregular rates of added materials, difficulties in scarifying, the 
need for continuous calibration of equipment, problems with the heating units 
and their need for adjustment. 
 
 Cold Central Plant Recycling (CCPR) 
Recycling of the asphalt layers is done in central plant mixing without application of 
heat, where the old pavements are milled and transferred to the plant. The Reclaimed 
Asphalt Pavement (RAP) is processed (if it is necessary) and mixed with the materials 
to be added and then transported directly to the project site for paving. Usually, this 
method is used to produce recycled materials for base courses.

this modification requires adding some scales, belts and electronic circuits. The 
Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement (RAP) is milled and transported to the central asphalt 
mix plant and can be processed at the mixer site if necessary and fed to the asphalt 
mixer by 10-25%. There are other types of asphalt plants (Continuous) that will 
produce asphalt mixture in a consistent run once it is started, and the production 
capacity ranges from 200-800 tons / hour. These plants include a modern technology 
for heating Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement (RAP), and its percentage can be increased 
with asphalt mixtures produced to reach up to 70%. 
The use of Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement (RAP) in central asphalt plants has many 
advantages, including: 
 Controlling the quality of aged asphalt mixtures and correcting their properties 
to ensure the equivalent performance of their conventional mixtures. 
 Improving and treating any defects that may exist in the underlying asphalt 
layers before paving new layers. 
 Giving the contractors an adequate opportunity to know and apply the 
technology of producing and paving asphalt mixtures that contain percentages 
of Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement (RAP). 
 Contractors do not need to purchase additional new paving equipment, as the 
paving is carried out with the same existing equipment and in the same 
methods familiar to the contractors (only the existing asphalt mix plants need 
to be modified). 
 The percentage of Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement (RAP) used is 10-25%, and the 
remaining amount of Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement (RAP) produced through 
maintenance projects will be stored at the asphalt mix plant and used in other 
projects.

with scarifying and the addition and mixing of new materials (aggregate / bitumen /

1 Introduction 
Roads in Saudi Arabia are constructed using Hot Mix Asphalt (HMA) and as the 
infrastructure ages, these roads must be maintained and rehabilitated. This 
maintenance work produces large amounts of Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement (RAP) that 
can be reused in the road network for repair, rebuild and maintenance. There are 
many factors that affect the use of Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement (RAP) in paving 
layers, but the main factors are the economic factor and the environmental factor. 
Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement (RAP) is a good alternative for raw materials because it 
reduces the use of aggregate and raw asphalt binder required in the production of 
asphalt mixtures, thus conserving resources. The use of Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement 
(RAP) also saves energy and reduces transportation costs required to obtain high-
quality raw materials. For the use of RAP to be successful, it must be economically 
and environmentally efficient, perform well and be just as efficient as conventional 
pavement. Current methods of reusing old paving layers includes the following:  
A. Hot Asphalt Pavement Recycling (HR) 
 Hot Central Asphalt Plant Recycling (HCPR) 
 Hot In-Place Recycling (HIR) 
 
B. Cold Asphalt Pavement Recycling (CR) 
 Cold Central Plant Recycling (CCPR) 
 Cold In-Place Recycling (CIR) 
  
 Hot Central Asphalt Plant Recycling (HCPR) 
The Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement (RAP) is mixed with new aggregate and bitumen to 
produce asphalt mixtures. This is done in ordinary asphalt mixing plants, noting that 
all asphalt mix plants of contractors working on projects of the Ministry of Transport 
and logistic services are batch plants with medium production capacity, ranging from 
80-250 tons/hour, these plants do not currently include any system for adding RAP 
and can be modified to produce asphalt mixtures that include proportions of RAP, and
